The Shanghai Concession Taxpayers Association sent a letter to the Municipal Government and a telegram to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs yesterday, requesting the recovery of roads built beyond the boundaries in West Shanghai by foreigners, and protested to the Municipal Council, requesting immediate return. The letters and telegrams are recorded as follows: ▲Letter to the Municipal Government: Respectfully, on the 15th of this month, the Municipal Council of the Public Concession infringed on our national sovereignty and hindered the Public Security Bureau from performing its duties on the roads built beyond the boundaries in West Shanghai, which is very distressing. The roads built beyond the boundaries by the Municipal Council have no legal basis. It is already wrong to delay the return to your government for management until now. Now, it wants to take further actions in an attempt to seize police power, which is even more intolerable. Director Yuan of the Public Security Bureau maintains police power and is loyal to the country, which is greatly admired. The association believes that in order to achieve a permanent solution, the Municipal Council should be requested to recover the roads built beyond the boundaries, so that all problems can be easily solved. It is reasonable to forward this letter to you, hoping that you will review and implement it.

▲致外交部電南京國民政府外交部王部長鈞鑒竊查上海公共租界工部局越界所築之路全無法律上之根據理應早日交于上海市政府管理至其路上警權歷由市公安局行使乃工部局忽于本月十五日派捕前往滬西越界所築之路上妨害市公安局行使公務殊屬侵犯我國主權曷勝痛心爲特電請鈞部提出收回越界築路之交涉以達一勞永逸之目的不勝企望之至上海租界納稅華人會叩宥印

▲Telegram to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs: To Minister Wang of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs of the National Government in Nanjing, greetings. It is found that the roads built beyond the boundaries by the Shanghai Public Concession Municipal Council have no legal basis at all. They should have been handed over to the Shanghai Municipal Government for management long ago. The police power on the roads has always been exercised by the Municipal Public Security Bureau. However, the Municipal Council suddenly sent police to the roads built beyond the boundaries in West Shanghai on the 15th of this month, hindering the Municipal Public Security Bureau from performing its duties, which is a great infringement on our national sovereignty and is very distressing. Therefore, a special telegram is sent to request your ministry to raise the issue of recovering the roads built beyond the boundaries in order to achieve a permanent solution. I am extremely hopeful. Shanghai Concession Taxpayers Association bows and apologizes.

▲致工部局函該會又致工部局總辦愛德華氏函云逕啟者案查越界築路爲貴局侵害我國主權而無法律根據行動之一種民國十四年五月三十日之慘案越界築路亦爲其發生原因之一路之建築旣無法律上之根據則路上警權自無行使之餘地蓋越界築路於法必須交回上海市政府管理而其路上之警權自應由上海市政府之公安局行使因之滬西各越界所築之路其行使警權者向爲市公安局詎料貴局突於十五日派捕侵犯市公安局滬西各路上警權之事幾於釀成重大之不幸事件本會不勝遺憾未便緘默相應函達至希查照除即行糾

▲Letter to the Municipal Council: The association also sent a letter to Mr. Edwards, Director General of the Municipal Council, saying: Respectfully, the construction of roads beyond the boundaries is an action of your bureau that infringes on our national sovereignty and has no legal basis. The tragic incident of May 30, 1925, was also caused by the construction of roads beyond the boundaries. Since the construction of the roads has no legal basis, there is no room for exercising police power on the roads. According to the law, the construction of roads beyond the boundaries must be returned to the Shanghai Municipal Government, and the police power on the roads should be exercised by the Public Security Bureau of the Shanghai Municipal Government. Therefore, the police power on the roads built beyond the boundaries in West Shanghai has always been exercised by the Municipal Public Security Bureau. Unexpectedly, your bureau suddenly sent police on the 15th to infringe on the police power of the Municipal Public Security Bureau on the roads in West Shanghai, which almost led to a major unfortunate event. This association is very regretful and cannot remain silent. A corresponding letter is sent to you, hoping that you will investigate and immediately correct this illegal action to avoid major disputes, and promptly return the roads built beyond the boundaries to the Shanghai Municipal Government to show respect for our national sovereignty and to demonstrate the sincerity of cooperation.

Methods for Paying Late Grain Tax Fines 142

Report from the County Finance Bureau

The Shanghai County Finance Bureau issued a public notice yesterday stating that on January 25th of this year, it received Instruction No. 161 from the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Finance, which stated that the Department had requested to reinstate the previous practice of imposing a 10% late payment fine on overdue grain taxes after two months from the start of collection, as was the case before the fifth year of the Republic (1916). The Provincial Government Committee had approved this matter at its 215th meeting and should be followed accordingly. In addition to issuing separate orders, the original request and concise rules should be copied and the bureau ordered to comply, post a public notice, and implement the rules starting from the grain tax collection of the 19th year of the Republic (1930), and report back for verification without fail. The lower bureau has received this instruction and, considering that the opening date for collecting the grain tax of the 19th year and the amount of late payment surcharges have already been announced, it is deemed appropriate to copy the concise rules again for public knowledge. It is hoped that all citizens of the county will pay at the counter within the two-month deadline to avoid being summoned for additional fines. This is hereby announced.

▲Concise Rules for Late Payment Fines: (1) All counties collecting grain tax and reed tax should follow the established practice before the fifth year of the Republic (1916), with a two-month deadline from the start of collection. A 10% late payment fine will be imposed for payments exceeding this deadline. (2) The late payment surcharge will be implemented after the two-month deadline from the start of the grain tax collection of the 19th year (1930). No extensions will be granted under any pretext. (3) The late payment fine will only apply to the regular provincial and county taxes. No surcharges will be imposed on any additional taxes collected concurrently. (4) Two months after the start of collection, each county should clearly demarcate the amounts collected for grain tax and reed tax and submit a report for auditing purposes. (5) All fines collected should be remitted to the province for use, as was the case before the fifth year of the Republic (1916). No county is allowed to retain any portion of the fines. (6) The old system of charging 20% for the first two months should be immediately abolished. (7) If payment is still not made one month after the penalty period, collection will be enforced.

Resolutions of the Rice Committee of the Citizens' Association 143

Investigating the Contents of the Municipal Council's Rice Purchase

And Preventing Rice Merchants from Hoarding and Profiteering

The Rice and Grain Issue Special Committee organized by the Shanghai Citizens' United Association held its first meeting at the Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday afternoon at 4 o'clock. The special committee members present were Yu Hualong, Zhang Yichen, Qiu Jialiang, Wu Liangsheng, Zhang Xianfang, Yu Yangsheng, Chen Jicheng, Chen Weiwen, Jiang Xinzhao, Hu Fengxiang, Zhang Hengbai, Yu Zhongcheng, and over ten other people. Committee Member Zhang Yichen was elected as chairman. After the formalities, the chairman reported that the Association had specially organized this special committee to study the issue of rice and grain supply, paying attention to people's livelihood and remedying the food shortage. The committee members bear a heavy responsibility, and they should strive for rigorous and rapid progress in their approach to avoid disappointing the citizens. After the report, the committee discussed the following agenda items: (1) Committee Member Jiang Xinzhao submitted a draft of eight articles for the committee's organizational regulations for public decision. The resolution was to adopt the draft proposed by Committee Member Jiang Xinzhao after reading and slightly revising each article. (2) The chairman proposed the election of standing committee members and a secretary. Zhang Yichen, Yu Hualong, Hu Fengxiang, Zhang Xianfang, and Yu Yangsheng were immediately elected as standing committee members, and Committee Member Jiang Xinzhao was elected as secretary. (3) Committee Member Qiu Jia proposed that although rice prices have recently fallen, most rice shops do not publicly display detailed daily rice prices, and there are instances of mixing inferior rice to reduce the quantity of rice sold. He proposed that the authorities be requested to issue an order requiring all rice shops to strictly comply. The resolution was to request the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs to issue an order requiring all rice merchants to display rice and grain prices daily and strictly prohibit the mixing of inferior rice, increasing the price through secret channels, or reducing the quantity of rice sold to uphold the law and reassure the people. (4) Committee Member Jiang Xinzhao proposed that the Municipal Council has agreed to allocate funds to purchase cheap rice to regulate rice prices. As a legal body representing the citizens in the area, should the Association send representatives to investigate the truth and assist in the process? The resolution was to appoint Committee Members Hu Fengxiang and Yu Yangsheng to first consult with Chinese Director Tan Qiqing to inquire about the truth and then verify it. (5) Jiang Xinzhao proposed that many foreign rice shipments have recently arrived, but because the Shanghai rice market has already fallen, many rice merchants are unwilling to sell and are storing the goods in warehouses and borrowing cash from banks and money houses to hoard and wait for an opportunity. This has a significant impact on rice prices and people's livelihoods. Should this be investigated and dealt with? The resolution was to assign the investigation to committee members separately and submit the evidence to the authorities for investigation and handling as soon as reliable evidence is obtained. (6) The meeting decided that the standing committee would meet every Friday at 3:00 PM, and standing committee members would be on duty at the meeting every day. (7) The committee requested that all members investigate and develop plans at any time. The meeting adjourned at 6 o'clock.

Record of the Joint Meeting of Surveillance Team Leaders of the Shanghai North Defense Corps 145

The Shanghai North District Defense Corps held a joint meeting of surveillance team leaders at 3 PM yesterday. All members were present. Corps Commander Wang presided, and Wu Fuchu served as recorder. After the usual formalities, the chairman reported the purpose of the meeting and declared that since the establishment of the Corps in the 13th year of the Republic (1924) until its reorganization this year, it had been divided into twelve teams with sufficient firearms. However, due to several wars and misunderstandings, the firearms had been confiscated repeatedly, and even when returned, the number was insufficient, resulting in a shortage of weapons and ammunition, which in turn reduced the number of voluntary members. This time, the Corps was ordered to reorganize according to the new regulations, with each team limited to 108 members. The corps has been reorganized into nine teams. Except for the ninth team, which is a reserve team, the other eight teams have been reorganized, and the number of members has been replenished according to the order. Currently, the Corps plans to pay attention to local defense because the war in the front is not yet over. Moreover, the defense corps is a popular self-defense organization that supplements the local police. However, according to the reports from each team, the number of firearms only accounts for half of the number of members. The strength is still insufficient, and it is still a matter of name only. The overall planning requires tens of thousands of dollars. The leaders and directors of various industries in Zhabei have made donations, but where it is insufficient, Committee Member Yu and Director Wang are requested to consult with public-spirited people in Shanghai to find ways to raise funds to achieve a large-scale arrangement to maintain local security. Therefore, today's meeting is convened to request that each surveillance team leader submit a register of directors to the Corps so that a meeting can be scheduled to raise funds. The meeting discussed several items related to the progress of team affairs and adjourned at 6 PM.

League of Nations Health Officer's Itinerary in Shanghai 147

Reuters, Shanghai, 28th: The port health officer sent by the League of Nations, who has been traveling in Singapore, Batavia, Saigon, Hong Kong, Guangzhou, and Unalaska, is now arriving in Shanghai aboard the President Taft. He is expected to arrive on the 31st of this month and plans to go to Japan the next day. Isolation specialists from Singapore, Java, Vietnam, Hong Kong, Siam, the Philippines, China, and Japan, led by Dr. Parker, director of the Isolation Department of the League of Nations Health Department, who was seconded by the Australian government, are traveling. The trip began on June 27th and is scheduled to end on August 12th. The purpose of this trip, organized by the League of Nations, is to enable the health officers to familiarize themselves with everything and the difficulties of each port and to assist in the coordination of isolation work. The itinerary of the members after arriving in Shanghai is as follows: 8:00 AM Arrive at the port on the 31st. 9:00 AM to 10:00 AM The Isolation Department's small boat will take the team to visit the disinfection machines in the river. 10:00 AM to Noon Visit various parts of the Huangpu River. 12:30 PM Luncheon at the Dongya Hotel at the invitation of Wu Liande. 2:00 PM to 5:00 PM Take a car to Wusong to visit the isolation hospital. 8:00 PM Dinner at the Dahua Hotel at the invitation of the Minister of Health. August 1st Morning rest. Noon Take the President Taft back to Japan.

Guangli Steamer Aground and Salvaged 148

▲The Guangli Steamer of China Merchants Bureau Aground at Grand Island. The Guangli steamer, originally a sea vessel, was transferred to the Yangtze River for use. It departed from Hankou on the 26th of this month and headed east towards Nanjing. Unexpectedly, it ran aground on the Yangtze River near Grand Island (approximately near Jiujiang). At that time, the tide was low, and the water depth in the river was only 11 feet. The Guangli steamer's draft was at least 14 feet, causing the hull to run aground on the Grand Island river surface, and the hull was stuck in the shallow sand and mud, making it impossible to move.

▲Request for Assistance by Telegram to Shanghai. The captain realized that reversing the engine could not move the hull and knew that it could not be rescued without towing. He sent a radio message to Shanghai requesting the Shanghai General Bureau to quickly send a ship with a draft of 11 feet to rescue. The message arrived in Shanghai on a Sunday. The head of the shipping department, upon receiving the report, immediately telegraphed Hankou, ordering the Jiangyu steamer, which had a shallower draft, to tow three barges to Grand Island for rescue.

▲Shallow Water Prevents Towing. The Jiangyu and three barges arrived at the grounding site to carry out the towing work, but the river water was too shallow, and the Guangli steamer's hull had already sunk into the shallow mud, making it impossible to tow it out for a while.

▲Appeal for Help from the Chief Mate. The Guangli has been aground for more than two days. The Jiangyu could not tow it out, and the Guangli steamer's chief mate has taken the dispatched rescue boat to Hankou to discuss rescue measures with the Hankou branch in order to return to tow the steamer.

Remarks by Han Yougang, Representative to the International Silk Conference, After Returning to China 149

The International Silk Conference was held in New York, USA, last autumn. China sent four representatives to attend. In addition to representatives Xue, Wang, and Li, who returned to China in succession last year, representative Han Yougang stayed in the United States for several months due to personal matters and was later dispatched by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to Belgium to participate in the International Exposition. He returned to China via Siberia yesterday. A reporter from the Guowen News Agency visited Mr. Han to discuss the conference. (Reporter) Mr. Han, could you tell us about the detailed situation of the International Silk Conference? (Han) The situation of the Silk Conference has been published in the newspapers by the representatives who returned to China last year, and my views are similar, so there is no need to repeat them. However, I hope that Chinese people will continue to improve silkworm breeding and silk reeling based on scientific methods. The future of silk is promising. (Reporter) You were dispatched by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to Belgium to participate in the Exposition. Could you tell us about the situation of the Exposition? (Han) After the Silk Conference last year, I wanted to investigate the government and industry and commerce in the United States, so I was unable to return to China with the other representatives. At the end of February of this year, I received an order from the Ministry to participate in the Exposition in Belgium. I left the United States in April and transferred from England to Belgium. First, I went to the north of Belgium. Because of domestic ethnic relations, the centennial exposition could not be held in one place. The north was in Antwerp, which is the coast of Belgium. The exposition there was dedicated to the products and navigation of the colonies of various countries.

The establishment had not been completed at that time, and the products and wax figures of men and women from the three northeastern provinces of China were displayed inside as colonial products and figures. The map on the wall depicted Japan and China in the same color. I witnessed this abominable situation. In addition to reporting everything to the Central Party Headquarters and the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, I also asked the Chinese ambassador to Belgium to fight for it. After repeated negotiations, the Japanese realized that they were wrong and moved all the items away. The exposition in the south was in Liège, the most developed industrial area in Belgium. The population is about 160,000. The venue is next to the Meuse River, about 200 acres in size. The area of our exhibition hall is only 300 square feet, which is very small. Furthermore, because the domestic industry and commerce were not willing to actively participate, the results were very unsatisfactory. If the items purchased and transported by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce had not been added, the situation would have been even more unbearable. (Reporter) You returned from Siberia this time, passing through Russia. Were you delayed? Could you tell us what you witnessed? (Han) When the train we were on entered Russian territory from Berlin via Poland, we had to change trains in Moscow for about eight hours. I spent five hours wandering the streets of the city. I saw hungry people everywhere, gathering in front of bakeries to receive black bread. As for the shops, nine out of ten were empty, and there was no commerce to speak of. The people walking on the road were all hungry and terrified. The train journey took eight days, and beggars were everywhere, and the people suffered unspeakably. And there are still scum among our Chinese youth who advocate communism, whose flesh is not enough to eat. (Reporter) You have temporarily left the Ministry of Industry and Commerce. Are you no longer serving in politics? (Han) I have realized deeply after returning from abroad this time. Although the trip lasted only eleven months and passed through only a dozen countries, the feelings were profound. I have decided to break away from everything and serve the country. I know that a country's standing on the earth requires a unified regime and a stable center to survive and prosper. I hope that all compatriots will rise up and work together to prevent our Chinese nation from becoming slaves in an irredeemable situation. At this point, Mr. Han sighed, and the reporter bid farewell and left.

Members of the Chinese Corps of the International Settlement Volunteer Corps Receive Awards 150

Silver Braids Are Hard to Obtain

The Chinese Corps of the International Settlement Volunteer Corps was initiated by Mr. Yu Qiaqing, starting with the Shanghai North Chinese Merchants' Gymnastics Association. Since joining the volunteer corps of the concession, they have consistently encouraged each other to serve with dedication and have always taken the lead in times of danger, striving for excellence. Therefore, they have been able to achieve good results over the years and are admired by the teams of various countries. It is heard that the corps headquarters presents a long-service medal to first-class qualified members who have served for twelve years. As previously reported, a silver braid is added to the top of the long-service medal for those who have served for seventeen years, and two silver braids are added for those who have served for twenty-two years to mark their many years of service and increase the honor of long service. However, this silver braid is not easy to obtain. It is not only based on years of service but also requires excellence in various courses, proficiency, and self-discipline over the years to achieve this. Therefore, looking around the entire corps, only ten people have double silver braids, two of whom are Chinese. Only Xu Tonghao and Hu Yunqiu have single silver braids. There are only twelve people in the entire corps, and five of them are Chinese, namely Song Yunqi, Liu Jinghe, Chong Dihua, Sun Zigao, and Chen Wenlong.

The First Batch of Released Vagrants from the Diligent Labor Institution for Vagrants 151

A Total of Thirty-Six People

The Shanghai Charity Organization established the Diligent Labor Institution for Vagrants. Since it began accepting vagrants in April of last year and reported its establishment to the Bureau of Social Affairs on June 11th, it has been one year since then. The institution has accepted more than 500 vagrants in succession. According to Article 7 of the institution's charter, vagrants who have served a full year and have shown evidence of repentance may be reported for release. The director of the institution, Wu Tang, will verify the families, origins, and the amount of work bonuses due to the vagrants who have served their terms and report them to the Bureau of Social Affairs and the Public Security Bureau for approval before releasing them. The release ceremony was held yesterday to show solemnity. Representatives from the Bureau of Social Affairs, Rao Qiangsheng, and the Public Security Bureau, Section Chief Huang of the Second Section, the section chief of the Third Sub-Bureau of the Sixth District, and the chairman of the institution's board of directors, Wang Yiting, the standing director, Qin Yanqi, and Yang Fuyuan, as well as dozens of guests from all walks of life, attended the ceremony. The meeting began at 10:00 AM. Director Wu reported on the progress of the past year and the conduct and work of the vagrants who were released after serving their terms. Representatives from the Bureau of Social Affairs, Rao, the Public Security Bureau, Huang, and the chairman of the board of directors, Wang Yiting, then gave speeches, generally stating that the reason why people become vagrants is due to their excessive dependence and lack of self-reliance, and that the way to be a good person should focus on the goodness of the heart. The released vagrants then gave a speech of thanks, which was quite pertinent and moved the audience. It is heard that the first batch of released vagrants totaled thirty-six people, and the total amount of work bonuses issued was more than 440 yuan. After the meeting, they took photos and thanked everyone before leaving.

Public Organizations in Wusong Request the Removal of District Chief Yang 152

The Wusong Eighth District Party Department sent a letter to Yuan, the Director of the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau, yesterday, stating that Wusong is adjacent to Shanghai and is related to the overall image of the city. The most important thing for the local area is police administration. The quality of the personnel of the police administration should be a matter of concern to the general public. Without discussing the quality of the police administration since District Chief Yang Maorong took office, his words and actions are absurd, his behavior is perverse, and he is selfish and does not conform to public opinion. In particular, a photo of him and a woman who jumped into the sea taken shoulder to shoulder has been circulating in society, causing shock and consternation. The newspapers have been reporting on it, and there is no way to hide it. If he is not punished, how can the officialdom be rectified? Moreover, the district chief is a model for the police personnel in the entire district, and he has openly taken this unexpected action. Speaking leniently, it can be said that it is not a matter of great importance, but in terms of personality, even small matters should be taken care of. If he is not investigated, I am afraid that the superiors will follow the example, and the future of the police administration will be unimaginable. Our department is in the same district and has closer ears and eyes. We have silently observed public sentiment and cannot bear to remain silent. Therefore, we have prepared a letter to inform you and dare to ask you to quickly remove him from his post and investigate him as a warning to others and to purify the officialdom.

More than ten public organizations, including the Wusong Chamber of Commerce, the Farmers' Association, the Seamen's Union, the Wusong Branch, the Lumber Merchants' Guild, and the Customs Brokers' Guild, sent a letter to Zhang, the Mayor of Shanghai, and Yuan, the Director of the Public Security Bureau, stating that since Yang Maorong, the district chief of the Seventh District of Public Security, took office, his handling of official affairs has been perverse. In the case of the woman who jumped into the sea, he openly took a photo with her. He did not avoid suspicion, and the district chief's personality has been lost, causing public opinion to be in an uproar. The Chamber of Commerce and other organizations are concerned about the future of the police administration and believe that the local morality is at stake and cannot remain silent. Therefore, we are informing you of the situation and requesting you to review and approve it and to quickly punish him as a warning to others and to maintain the police administration.

Old Farmer Dies Tragically in Houjiazhai 155

Sun Laowu's Death Is Extremely Tragic

The Nephew Who Fled Is Suspected of Killing His Uncle

A murder case occurred in Houjiazhai, near Jiangwan, yesterday morning. The deceased, Sun Junbao, was from Tongzhou and was 50 years old. His death was extremely tragic. He was forcibly chopped and stabbed with a hoe-like sharp blade and scissors. The murderer fled after the incident. Only one suspected accomplice was arrested. According to the deceased's nephew, his cousin is strongly suspected of killing his uncle. If so, it would be another major case of patricide.

▲The Smell of Blood in the Thatched Hut. The deceased, Sun Junbao, also known as Lao Wu, lived in a thatched hut behind Houjiazhai. He lived alone because he was old and weak and unable to work. He planted vegetables behind the house to make a living. At around 5 AM yesterday morning, a carpenter named Jiang went to knock on the door. After a long time, there was no response. He then pushed the door open and suddenly smelled a strong smell of blood. He was shocked and, upon closer inspection, saw Sun Laowu lying stiff on the ground, covered in blood. He was extremely frightened and ran back to report to the police. The patrol leader of the Qiaojiaqiao Police Station in the Fifth District of the Public Security Bureau went to the thatched hut to investigate and saw blood flowing around the deceased like a river, all red. A small half of his head had been chopped off, his cheeks were flattened, and his teeth were visible. There were huge wounds on his left ribs, chest, and back. The fingers of his left hand had been chopped off with a knife. His body was lying on the ground, struggling before death. The murder weapon seemed to be a hoe-like tool.

▲No Children Under His Knee, Taking His Nephew as a Son. The reason for Sun Laowu's murder is quite complicated. According to his nephew, Sun Fusheng, his cousin Sun Liansheng is strongly suspected of killing his uncle. The deceased was half a century old and lost his wife ten years ago. He had no children under his knee. Three years ago, he adopted Sun Zulilai, the fourth son of his third brother Sun Xuewen, as his heir. Zulilai was young and not used to living with Sun Laowu. Before long, he returned to Tongzhou and severed the relationship between adoptive father and son. Sun Laowu then adopted Liansheng, Zulilai's brother, as his son. Liansheng is now 26 years old and married with children. When he was adopted by Sun Laowu, his wife also came with him.

▲The Adopted Son Is Unruly and Sent Back to His Hometown. Sun Liansheng has always been unruly. Last year, he came to Shanghai with his wife and lived with Sun Laowu in Houjiazhai. Because he had no job, Sun bought a rickshaw and ordered him to pull it to make a living. Sun Liansheng was lazy and fond of gambling. He spent all the money he earned and associated with bad friends, neglecting his wife and children. Sun Laowu was even more unable to get support from him and was very angry. A month ago, he decided to send Sun Liansheng and his wife back to their hometown and sever the relationship between adoptive father and son. Who knew that Sun Liansheng would secretly return to Shanghai not long after returning to Tongzhou, about half a month ago.

▲Stealing Money and Selling the Rickshaw Angers the Old Man. After Sun Liansheng returned to Shanghai, he went to his uncle Sun Laowu again. At first, Sun Laowu did not give him a good face. Because he was disturbed, he reluctantly allowed him to stay. Who knew that his nature was hard to change and he eventually made friends with bandits. He stole Sun Laowu's savings and, not satisfied, stole the rickshaw and sold it privately. When the matter was revealed, Sun Laowu paid money to redeem it and severely reprimanded Liansheng. Liansheng's six or seven bandit friends harbored ill intentions towards Sun Laowu and made threatening remarks.

▲Complaining to His Nephew, He Died the Next Day. Sun Fusheng, Sun Laowu's eldest nephew, works as a driver at Huifeng Motors at No. 136 Laotaiping Lane, Waitan, Nanshi. Two days ago, Sun Laowu went to visit him. After meeting, he said to Sun, "Liansheng is becoming increasingly degenerate. His six or seven friends all harbor ill intentions towards me. I am afraid for my life." Sun Fusheng comforted his uncle with kind words. Who knew that Sun Laowu would be murdered the next day, which made him believe that his nephew Sun Liansheng was the main culprit in this case, motivated by money.

▲Seeking Help from Neighbors, an Accomplice Is Arrested. According to the deceased's neighbors, Sun had been quite distraught for several days before his death and often sought help from his neighbors, saying, "I am old and afraid of being harmed. Please watch over me day and night." The neighbors were surprised by his words and often privately discussed his change in attitude. After the incident, Sun Liansheng disappeared. The police arrested Ji Shuangquan, a rickshaw puller suspected of being an accomplice, for questioning.

A Large Fire in Broad Daylight at the End of Linping Road 156

More Than Thirty Houses Destroyed

An Eighty-Year-Old Man Burned

Yesterday afternoon at approximately 2:50 PM, a fire suddenly broke out in the shacks and bungalows at the end of Linping Road, south of Hujia Muqiao Road, and near Taiping Bridge in northern Shanghai. Approximately thirty houses were destroyed, and an eighty-year-old man from Gaoyou named Wu Wanxing was severely burned. Details are as follows:

▲ The Fire Scene: The fireground was roughly square-shaped. The shacks and bungalows that were engulfed were surrounded by tiled houses and multi-story buildings. The affected area was accessed via Xiang'an Lane, which was extremely narrow. Going north from Xiang'an Lane was Hujia Muqiao Road, beyond the bridge was Miaodong Road. Linping Road was opposite Miaodong Road, separated by a small river. Water for extinguishing the fire was drawn from this river, as the area had no running water or artesian wells, and residents relied on the river for drinking water. The number of houses damaged, from east to west, was as follows: approximately ten shacks, eleven rooms of the Sanxinli building (house numbers 7 to 17, with 16 and 17 being partially destroyed), six and a half bungalows from 6 to 12 Xiang'an Lane (except for 12, which was half-destroyed, the rest suffered significant damage), and three and a half bungalows of Yongxiang Lane near Taiping Bridge Road (house numbers 30 to 32). The fireground was surrounded by houses, resulting in few exits. The only one was Xiang'an Lane which connects to Hujia Muqiao Road shaped like a bottleneck. Therefore, after the fire started, escaping was difficult, and the fire brigade struggled to extinguish the flames. Furthermore, due to the lack of nearby water mains, the hoses had to be extended a considerable distance into the river. Fortunately, yesterday's high tide and rapid current helped maintain water pressure, otherwise even more houses would have been destroyed.

▲ Cause of the Fire: After the fire started, the various fire brigades in Zhabei rushed to the scene and tried their best to extinguish the flames. However, due to the narrow space, crowds, and difficulty in drawing water, they initially struggled. It was not until the shacks were completely burned down that the fire gradually subsided. By the time the fire was extinguished, it was already late. All that was left on the fireground were piles of charred wood and broken tiles. When the firefighters were working, police officers from the Linping Road Police Station of the Fifth District, Third Precinct were on the scene to maintain order. The suspected cause of the fire was that the couple Wu Daguozi, from Yancheng, stated under questioning that the fire was started by their five-year-old daughter, Chundi, who was cooking lilies and caused a fire. The couple was away at work and did not take care of the house. After the fire started, their daughter, Chundi, panicked and ran away and is still missing. The severely burned elderly man, Wu Wanxing from Gaoyou, lived in a shack in Sanxinli, Hujia Muqiao Road. Due to his old age and frailty, he suffered severe burns. Afterwards, he was taken by police car to Tongren Hospital for treatment, his condition is precarious.

Detective Arrests Xia Wenlin 157

Three Robberies at Tongan Factory

Arrested After Long Surveillance on Binlang Road

Yesterday, the Detective Team of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, together with Chinese and Western detectives from the Putuo Road Police Station, successfully cracked the case of the robbery at the Tongan Fabric Factory near the New Pier in Nanshi on the 23rd of this month, during which a firearm was seized from the patrol officer guarding the First District Headquarters. The main perpetrator, Xia Wenlin, has been apprehended. The details of the investigation are recorded as follows:

▲ Three Robberies, Binding of Police, and Seizing of Firearms: On the 12th of the previous month at 4:00 PM, the Tongan Fabric Factory near the New Pier in Nanshi was suddenly robbed by four thieves, who made off with over three thousand dollars in cash. Incredibly, twenty-seven days later, on the 28th of the previous month, the factory was robbed again, this time of over one hundred dollars. Finally, on the 23rd of this month, the thieves came for the third time. Although the loss was only ten dollars in cash and a few dimes, the patrol officer stationed there was bound and had his pistol stolen.

▲ Police Bureau Orders Intensified Investigation: To avoid the thieves becoming more emboldened after the incident, the case was not reported in the newspapers. Yuan Liang, the Director of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, took the matter very seriously and immediately ordered his subordinates to solve the case within a certain timeframe. After receiving this order, Lu Ying, the Captain of the Detective Team, secretly instructed his officers to intensify the investigation.

▲ Main Culprit Xia Wenlin: Two days later, detective team members Qi Haitian, Shan Bin, Fu Kezhong, Xu Rong, Miao Jinhai, etc., received a tip that the mastermind behind the robberies was Xia Wenlin, a native of Anhui who had dealings with the factory. Xia now owns a small weaving factory named Xia Wenji on Binlang Road in the International Settlement. All the goods produced are sold to Tongan, so Xia is fully aware of the prices Tongan pays its customers every day. It was reported that the four thieves who went there the first time (June 12th) were sent by Xia, so they were asked to arrest him as soon as possible.

▲ Detectives Lay in Wait for Three Days and Two Nights: At the same time, Shen Chongli, a Chinese detective from the Gordon Road Police Station, received a tip that Xia was also behind the theft from the home of Wang Zhenshou, a former commander in Hankou, several months ago on Jing'an Temple Road, where over three thousand dollars were stolen. Therefore, detectives from both sides disguised themselves and laid in wait at the location for three days and two nights. Finally, at 7:30 AM yesterday, Xia was apprehended inside a "tiger stove" at 340 Binlang Road.

▲ Temporarily Detained at the Police Station, Awaiting Extradition: After being apprehended, Xia was transferred to the Xinzha Police Station for temporary detention. After a thorough questioning by the police chief, he was ordered to be returned to custody. It is reported that Captain Lu has already reported the details of the case to Director Yuan, and plans to prepare a letter within the next few days to request extradition for trial.

Municipal Public Security Bureau Inspector Ling Runxiang Assassinated 158

Shot and Killed in an Alley

Cause Still Unknown

At approximately 11:15 PM last night, an assassination occurred at the entrance of Dexing Lane on North Jiangxi Road in Hongkou. The victim was Ling Runxiang, an incumbent inspector at the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau's Inspectorate. Ling had finished work and returned home around 4:00 PM yesterday afternoon. Around 11:00 PM, he left his concubine's residence in Dexing Lane and was assassinated by an enemy at the entrance of the alley, suffering a fatal gunshot wound to the head. The assailant escaped without a trace. Details are as follows:

▲ Former Chinese Detective at the Police Station: Ling Runxiang, a native of Panyu, Guangdong, was 36 years old. He lived in Taihua Lane on North Jiangxi Road and had a concubine residing at 634 Dexing Lane. Three years ago, Ling was a Chinese detective at the Hongkou Police Station. After the May 30th Incident, he left his position as a detective. In 1928, when Dai Shifu was the Director of the Public Security Bureau, Ling joined the Bureau as an investigator. Last year, he transferred to the Inspectorate and was promoted to inspector. He was known for his resolute manner and was highly regarded by Inspector He.

▲ Assailant Escaped the Scene: Last night, Ling had dinner at his concubine's residence in Dexing Lane. Around 11:00 PM, he announced that he was going out. His concubine accompanied him to the entrance of the alley, where he was suddenly attacked. According to eyewitnesses, Ling Runxiang was chatting happily with his concubine just minutes before the attack and appeared to be reluctant to leave. As Ling stepped out of the alley, a man wearing a gray long gown approached him head-on. Just as Ling turned to look, gunshots rang out. Ling was shot and fell to the ground. After killing Ling, the assailant ran back into the alley and disappeared shortly after.

▲ Fatal Gunshot to the Head: After being shot, Ling's body fell at the entrance of the west alley of Dexing Lane, attracting a large crowd of onlookers. He was lying on his back, with his head to the north and feet to the south, with his hands pressed against his abdomen, as if in great pain. There was a bullet hole below his left eye, the flesh was mangled, and blood flowed everywhere. Because his skull was shattered and his brain matter was spilling out, he could not be saved. After hearing the news, the Hongkou Police Station immediately dispatched detectives to the scene to apprehend the assailant and transported the body to the morgue for examination.

▲ Two Theories on the Reason for the Assassination: Although the reason for Ling's assassination can be speculated, there are many clues, making it difficult to pinpoint a single cause. Some say that Ling had considerable influence in the Hongkou area and was involved in matters related to gambling clubs, which may have caused him to make enemies. Others say that after Ling joined the Public Security Bureau, his work may have offended factions within the opposition, leading to him being targeted unknowingly by his enemies. Both theories are presented as possible explanations for Ling's death.

▲ Stray Bullet Injures Elderly Woman: It was said that Ling Runxiang was also carrying a handgun for self-defense, but it was of no use to him. A stray bullet struck Wu Shenshi, the owner of the Wu Yuanchang tobacco and paper shop, injuring her head. The bullet entered below her eye, causing severe injuries. She was taken to Tongren Hospital for treatment by police car.

Young Man and Woman Commit Suicide by Drowning in the Sea Together 159

Bodies Discovered in Wusong

Hao, a 36-year-old man from Huai'an, worked as a teacher in Shanghai. He was reserved and rarely smiled. In January of this year, Hao met a woman named Fu Yushi in the French Park. Ms. Fu, 38 years old and from Nanxiang, was beautiful and well-educated. Her husband, Mr. Fu, had been sent on a military expedition years ago and is now stationed in Guangzhou. Ms. Fu's husband was far away and unable to return, she felt restless and unable to control herself. Hao and Fu Yushi met unexpectedly and immediately connected with each other. Over time, they became intimate and engaged in illicit behavior. They rented a house together at the bottom of Dapu Bridge in the French Concession and opened a small restaurant, with Fu Yushi in charge of everything. However, after the restaurant opened, business was slow, and they suffered significant losses, accumulating debt. By the end of last month, the restaurant could no longer be sustained and had to be closed. Creditors, seeing the closure of the restaurant, repeatedly pressed the couple for payment. Hao and Fu Yushi were unable to cope and arranged to settle all debts by the end of the month. On the 25th of this month, Fu Yushi went around borrowing over 250 dollars from friends and relatives. However, that night, while Hao and Fu Yushi were chatting, they inadvertently mentioned that Hao had once won over a thousand dollars in a single night at a roulette table. The two became greedy and immediately hired a rickshaw to take the 250 dollars they had borrowed during the day to a gambling den near Dongxin Bridge to make a final gamble. Unexpectedly, within an hour, all 250 dollars were lost. After returning home, they blamed each other. Realizing that the end of the month was approaching and they were unable to pay their debts, they became deeply saddened and decided to commit suicide. The previous morning, they wrote several suicide notes and mailed them to friends and relatives, expressing their feelings and announcing their intention to drown themselves in the sea at Wusong. In the afternoon, the two took a train to the seaside of Paotaiwan in Wusong. While no one was around, they held hands and drowned themselves in the sea. Around 7:00 PM that afternoon, a patrol boat from the Wusong Port Life Saving Bureau recovered a male corpse wearing a snow-flake woolen Zhongshan suit and yellow leather shoes in the middle of the breakwater at Paotaiwan. As the body was unidentified, the Bureau filled out a corpse tag and sent it to the morgue for encoffining. Around 8:00 AM yesterday morning, Hao and Ms. Yu's friends and relatives received the suicide notes and immediately went to the Wusong Life Saving Bureau to inquire. They confirmed that the two had indeed committed suicide. Later, Ms. Fu Yushi's body was also discovered on the bank of Yinhangpu at 11:00 AM yesterday morning. Her friends and relatives purchased a coffin and took her to the Siming Public Association for temporary storage, and reported to the Hao family in Huai'an to quickly come to Shanghai to handle the funeral arrangements.

Xi Ehan's Land Rent Brokerage Lawsuit 161

Closing Arguments

Xi Ehan leased over seven mu of land located in the middle section of Zhejiang Road to Huang Chujiu for the construction of buildings. Since the lease agreement was established on August 1st of last year, a series of lawsuits have arisen. Initially, the tenants there filed a lawsuit against Xi, then Xi and Huang sued each other. Now, Chen Guifu, the broker who acted as the middleman for the land lease, is suing Xi for embezzling his due share.

Initially, Chen Guifu and Kong Jingqing introduced Huang Chujiu to Xi Ehan. After several negotiations, an annual rent of 72,500 taels and a lease term of 20 years were agreed upon, totaling 1.45 million taels in rent. The agreed-upon brokerage fee was 2%, amounting to 29,000 taels. Kong Jingqing, as the middleman for Huang Chujiu, was to receive half of the amount, totaling 14,500 taels. Chen Guifu, as the middleman for Xi Ehan, was to receive the other half, but he did not receive a single penny. He later learned that Xi had taken it all, so Chen sued Xi for embezzlement. Xi firmly denied this, stating that the agreed-upon brokerage fee was calculated at 2.5% of the total rent for 20 years, with 1% going to the brokers on both sides, 1% to the landlord's accounting department, and the remaining 0.5% to the tenant's accounting department. Chen's share was not embezzled by him. Therefore, he also retained lawyers Jiang Yiping and Qin Liankui for his defense. Yesterday morning, Judge Zhou continued the hearing, summoning land broker Liu Hongsheng, who had been involved in the matter, to testify. Liu testified that Chen Guifu received over 8,000 taels of the brokerage fee from the landlord's side, while he received nothing. He had sued Chen in the local court in the city and received 600 dollars to settle the matter. Zhou, the accountant for Xi Ehan, also testified that his accounting department received 14,500 taels for the brokerage fee, and Kong also received 14,500 taels. The remaining 0.5% was received by Huang Chujiu's accounting department. Kong Jingqing testified that as Huang's middleman, he should have received 14,500 taels, while Chen, as Xi's middleman, did not actually receive any money. Chen was later sued by Liu, and he gave him 400 dollars to settle the case. Although the initial receipt stated that the brokerage fee was 2.5%, Huang only agreed to pay 2%, so the receipt was not valid. Huang Chujiu arrived at the court after 11:00 AM. He testified that the brokerage fee was indeed only 2%, with half going to the middleman on the landlord's side and half to the middleman on the tenant's side. His accounting department did not receive anything. Before the brokerage fee for Xi Ehan's side was paid, Xi's second concubine called his family and told them not to pay it to his accounting department. Therefore, he prepared a check for 14,500 taels on the day of the signing. When it came time to sign, Xi demanded that the brokerage fee for his side be paid to him, otherwise he would not sign. He then handed the check to Xi. The plaintiff, Chen Guifu, was indeed the initial introducer of this matter and had come to his house once. At the end, the lawyers on both sides made their closing arguments, and the court announced that a verdict would be delivered at a later date.

Gun and Ammunition Hidden in Ceramic Basin 164

▲Selling Old Goods Turns Out to be Selling Guns and Ammunition

▲Chasing Robbers Turns Out to be Chasing Gun Traffickers

Yesterday morning around 8:00 AM, Yan Huating, a police officer from the Second Watch Post of the First Precinct of the Second District of Shenxiang Pavilion in Nanshi, was on duty in Zhangchuan Old Lane when he noticed a crowd gathered in front of the Changtai Brick and Tile Shop at number 40. They were focused on a man buying old goods. Before long, someone suddenly shouted "Thief!" The old goods buyer and another person abandoned their load of old goods and fled, pursued by several people. After turning south onto Houjia Road, they fled to the front of the police station. Chief Qian, who was in the office, heard the commotion and immediately ordered Patrol Leader Wang Zhongqing to cooperate with Jiang Xiling, a police officer from the First Watch Post in front of the station, to intercept the suspects. After pursuing them to Hengde Lane, they apprehended the two men and brought them and the pursuers to the station. After questioning, Chief Qian learned from the pursuers that they saw the two men whispering to each other by the side of the road. Then, they saw that one of the men was carrying a stack of ceramic basins containing guns and ammunition, so they shouted "Thief!" Chief Qian then ordered Patrol Leader Wang to immediately go to the Changtai Brick and Tile Shop at number 40 of Zhangchuan Old Lane and bring back the abandoned load of old goods and stack of ceramic basins. After carefully examining them, they indeed found two Browning pistols, numbers 131004 and 231010, and 189 rounds of ammunition hidden in the ceramic basins. The method of concealment was quite clever. There were a total of twenty ceramic basins, but only the top and bottom ones were intact. The centers of the other eighteen basins were removed, and the guns and ammunition were hidden in the empty space. The stack was then tied with hemp rope in a cross pattern to make it look inconspicuous. It is unknown how a passerby discovered this and led to their arrest. Upon questioning, one of the defendants identified himself as Zhao Rugen, 45 years old, from Zhenjiang, residing at 104 Yanhai Lane, and a buyer of old goods. He stated that one of the men approached him and offered to sell a stack of ceramic basins for 1.40 dollars. He was about to pay when someone suddenly shouted "Thief!" He claimed to have no knowledge of the guns. The other defendant identified himself as Zhang Xilang, 40 years old, from Chongming, residing in the Wengjia Lane in Nanshi. He stated that he bought a stack of twenty ceramic basins in a porridge shop this morning for 2.40 dollars, and was intending to sell them when he was arrested, but he had no knowledge of the hidden weapons. Chief Qian, based on the fact that Zhang Xilang bought the basins for 2.40 dollars but was willing to sell them for only 1.40 dollars, suspected that there was something else going on. Due to the case involving hidden weapons, he prepared a document to transfer the suspects and the seized items to the Judicial Section for further investigation.

Contraband Hidden in Zhengda Steamer's Wooden Planks

Seeking Divorce Due to a Hidden Ailment 167

Wang Shiqing's Weak Body and Seminal Emission

Wu Muying's Mental Anguish

Local young woman Wu Muying (also known as Wang Wu's wife), is currently twenty years old. In the autumn of last year, she married Wang Shiqing. However, Wang suffers from a hidden ailment, leading to a marriage in name only, with no conjugal relations. For the sake of her lifelong happiness, Wu Muying has hired lawyer Wang Yanlun to file for divorce in the local court and request alimony. Her statement roughly states: The plaintiff, in September of last year, married the defendant Wang Shiqing under the arrangement of her parents, mediated by He Fufu, Zhang Songquan, Zhang Sihai, and others. Only after the marriage did she discover that the defendant suffered from a disability. The plaintiff did not wish to be his spouse, but the defendant concealed it deeply, forbidding any disclosure. The plaintiff was also ashamed to speak of it. It was not until she returned to Ningbo in March of this year that she confided in her parents. When questioned, they claimed they were unaware at the time and would never have acted as matchmakers if they had known beforehand. The plaintiff's parents, unclear about the truth, agreed with the defendant on a date to visit a doctor for examination. The defendant, however, preemptively consulted a doctor who stated that his vital energy was weak, he was incapable of sexual intercourse, he could not achieve an erection, he experienced seminal emission at the sight of a woman, his penis was small, there was no hope for offspring, this condition was incurable, and he had been suffering from chronic deficiency and depletion for a long time. This proves that the defendant has a long-standing incurable disability. According to current laws, if either party has a disability or illness at the beginning of an engagement, both families must be clearly notified and each should act according to their wishes. Otherwise, the marriage is unlikely to be fully valid, whether or not they are already married. The other party is entitled to request annulment or divorce. This has already been established as a precedent by the Supreme Court (see Case No. 23, Shang Zi, Year 17). Now, the defendant has a long-standing disability and did not provide clear notification at the time of the engagement or obtain the consent of the other party. Although they are already married, divorce should be granted according to precedent. Furthermore, the defendant does not fulfill his conjugal duties to the plaintiff, providing only the bare minimum of food. If unexpected guests arrive, he would give the food meant for the plaintiff to them, ignoring her hunger. Since the plaintiff returned to Ningbo, she has been refused entry back home, which is equivalent to abandonment, disregarding her livelihood. In terms of daily treatment, there is no affection and it is difficult to grow old together, so divorce should be granted. The reason for this divorce request originates with the defendant, and the plaintiff feels deeply mentally distressed. Moreover, she has no means of support after the divorce. At the very least, she should be paid a one-time alimony of 280 yuan to maintain her livelihood. Yesterday at 9 a.m., Judge Du specially opened the Second Court to hear the case. Both parties complied with the summons and appeared in court. The plaintiff, Wu Muying, wore a printed white Indian silk qipao, had short hair, and wore white silk shoes with red flowers and white socks. She was of medium height and had a pleasing appearance. The defendant, Wang Shiqing, wore a short shirt and trousers made of dark glossy silk, iron-machine satin shoes, had short hair in a flat-top style, and was short and stout with a purplish complexion, not appearing to suffer from a debilitating disease. After the judge took his seat, Wu Muying testified first, stating that she was 20 years old, from Shanghai, and currently residing at her mother's home at No. 830 Hengtai Lane, Zhoujiazui Road, Hongkou. (Question) When did you get married? (Answer) September 21st of last year. (Question) When did you return to Ningbo? (Answer) March 25th of this year. (Question) Why are you suing your husband? (Answer) I am requesting a divorce. (Question) Is it because of illness that you are seeking divorce? (Answer) Yes. At this point, the plaintiff's lawyer, Mr. Wang, presented the doctor's examination report and the defendant's handwritten letter to the court for inspection. After reviewing them, the judge ordered the defendant, Wang Shiqing, to testify. He stated that he was 28 years old, from Shangyu, Shaoxing, residing at No. 8, workshop of the Huafeng Yarn Factory in Wusong, and currently working as an electrician. (Question) What illness do you suffer from? (Answer) Since I was 24 years old, I have suffered from seminal emission. It continues to this day, and I have two or three wet dreams every month. (Question) How much do you earn each month? (Answer) At most, 33

Page 16

dollars, at least 22 or 23 dollars. (Question) Can your illness be cured? (Answer) I have seen a doctor, and they said it could be cured, but I don't have the money for treatment. (Question) How did your illness start? (Answer) According to the doctor, it's because my body is weak, so after working hard during the day, I often have wet dreams and seminal emission. (Question) Who did you consult? (Answer) Dr. Ma Xiangsi at Daqing Lane in the New World. (Question) She wants a divorce, what are your thoughts? (Answer) I don't want it. When I married her, we spent 916 yuan together. It's not easy for a craftsman like me to marry a wife. (Question) Your illness won't get better if you don't treat it. (Answer) I need to treat it. After obtaining the testimony, the judge told the plaintiff's lawyer, "It would be best to settle this case out of court." Lawyer Wang said, "My lawyer previously notified the defendant, asking him to come for a settlement, but he never came, so we filed the lawsuit." The judge then instructed them to attempt an out-of-court settlement within ten days. If no settlement is reached, another hearing will be scheduled and a judgment will be made according to the law. The court was then adjourned.

Enticing His Daughter and Coveting Her Property 168

Greedy Xu Yinru

Furious Zhu Musheng

Zhu Musheng, a farmer from the 90th District of Nanhui, Pudong, is over fifty years old. He owns several acres of land, enough to live comfortably. He is a small, well-to-do farmer. However, he has no sons, causing him anxiety like Bo Dao [a figure in Chinese history known for having no heir]. He only has three daughters. The two eldest daughters are already married. The third daughter, named A Wugu, is twenty-nine years old and has a beautiful appearance, a demure young lady. Her parents cherish her as the apple of their eye, intending to choose a good husband to marry into the family, inherit the family property, and continue the family line. Therefore, they are very strict in choosing a husband, and no one has been selected yet. Xu Yinru from Fengxian, who works as a tailor, is currently in his twenties. He is a licentious man. He learned that the Zhu family was well-off and that A Wugu was young and beautiful, so he used tailoring as an excuse to secretly seduce her. Wugu had no men around and little knowledge of the world, so she was eventually tempted by him and fell in love. This summer, Xu even incited Wugu to abscond to Shanghai with clothing and cash, staying in a hotel for over a month. Although Zhu discovered that his beloved daughter had been abducted by Xu, he dared not pursue the matter in Shanghai because Xu was associated with a "leader" and associated with ruffians. Unexpectedly, Xu, not content with what he had, sent a letter to the girl's parents, Zhu Musheng, the other day, forcing them to acknowledge him as their official son-in-law and inherit their property. Zhu was furious after reading the letter. He has already found out where Xu is hiding and hired a lawyer to file a complaint with the local court, requesting that the case be thoroughly investigated immediately to deter abduction and seduction.

Roulette Gambling on Avenue Edouard VII 169

Over Forty People Arrested

Gambling Ring Leader Fined Two Thousand Yuan

Wang Baohe from Suzhou recently set up a private roulette gambling den at a building on Avenue Edouard VII in the French Concession, gathering people to gamble and profiting from skimming, in violation of the ban. Detectives of the French Police Department, including Chief Inspector Shen Defu, Inspector Chen Sanlin, Detective Lu Jinchen, and Detectives Jiang Changwen and Ni Xiafei, discovered this. The other day, they moved silently and arrested over forty gamblers, seizing roulette gambling equipment, dominoes, dice, and 5,752 yuan in cash. The owner was brought to the police station along with the gamblers. After questioning them, the police chief ordered the gamblers to be lightly fined and released. Wang was released on bail. Yesterday, he was brought to the French court for investigation. First, the Western Detective Chief went to court, reported the situation, and presented the gambling equipment and cash to the court. When questioned, Wang Baohe confessed to setting up a private gambling den, gathering gamblers, and skimming profits. The Chinese and Western judges sentenced Wang to a fine of 2,000 yuan to be confiscated as a warning. The gambling equipment was destroyed and the cash was confiscated.

Countrymen Turning into Tragedy 170

Ding Xianchun Kicks Li Jizhong to Death

Ding Xianchun from Shandong came to Shanghai last month to seek employment and stayed at the home of his fellow villager, Li Jizhong, at No. 256 Huade Road. Li runs a pancake stall. Ding, having stayed for a long time, occasionally helped with the work. Last Saturday at 8 a.m., Ding and Li went out together. When they reached the Linqing Road Bridge, an argument suddenly broke out. Li accused Ding of stealing four yuan in cash from him. Ding angrily slapped Li in the face, and they started fighting each other. Ding's scrotum was kicked by Li, causing injury that could not be cured, and he died shortly after. The police station in charge arrested Li. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the Special District Local Court, where he was interrogated by Judge Feng Shide. The police station presented four yuan and twenty cents in cash found on the deceased's body as evidence. According to Li's confession, it was just a joke at the time. Who knew that the deceased would become angry out of shame? He also denied kicking. However, the police lawyer, Zhang Tianyin, claimed that according to the doctor's examination, the deceased's genitals were severely injured, indicating that he was indeed kicked. Judge Feng ordered the defendant to be remanded in custody, awaiting sentencing at a later date.

Tang Zhang's Suicide by Drinking Nitric Acid 171

The Result of Marital Discord

Feng Zhongcai from Fenghua, Ningbo, residing at No. 78, New Qiujiang Road, Zhabei, married Zhang. She is currently twenty-three years old. Their relationship was not very harmonious, and they often argued. The other day, they quarreled again over a trivial matter. Feng left in a fit of pique, declaring that he would never return home. After her husband left, Zhang, feeling that life was meaningless, became despondent and privately drank a small amount of nitric acid used in the factory, committing suicide. She died from poisoning immediately. Her family reported the incident to the police station in charge, who ordered a guarantor to report it to the local court. Yesterday afternoon, a prosecutor was dispatched to the scene to conduct an examination, confirming the cause of death and ordering the family to prepare a coffin for burial pending verification.

Sentenced to Compensation of One Hundred and Fifty Yuan

Yu Axiang is currently sixty-three years old. His son is unfilial. After getting married, he left home and never returned. Axiang had a wife and no means of living, so he worked as a peddler to make a living. The other day, at 7:20 a.m., he was carrying a load of eggs when he arrived at Tiantong Road near North Sichuan Road. As he was crossing the road from the north side to the south side, a truck with license number 16896 was driving from east to west and hit Yu, crushing his face and feet. He was bleeding profusely immediately. A detective saw this and sent him to the Tongren Hospital in the car. Because of his old age and blood loss, he died. He died at the hospital at 12:50 a.m. that evening. A Chinese detective from the Hongkou Police Station went to investigate and verified the facts. The body was taken to the autopsy center. Yesterday morning, the Special District Court commissioned Prosecutor Xu to examine the body, took a seat in the courtroom, asked Yu Zhang, the deceased's wife, a few questions, and then determined that the deceased, Yu Axiang, had indeed been hit and killed by a truck. According to the report and the circumstances of the statements, both sides were at fault. The car driver, Li Meiyou, was ordered to pay 150 yuan in compensation. The body was handed over to the deceased's family, Yu Zhang, to receive. If she is not satisfied, she can file a lawsuit in court.

A coolie on Avenue Edouard VII suddenly collapsed yesterday, his face changing drastically. He immediately took Positive Cross Oil from his person and rubbed it on the coolie's head and abdomen, and used chopsticks to pry open his mouth and poured the oil down. Within minutes, the coolie's limbs twitched, he vomited accumulated filth, and after a while he stood up, bowed and left.

Zhu Guishou is Punished for Fraud 178

Ruffians Dare to Fleece a Hotel Guest

Wang Yonggen originally ran a teahouse in a town in western Shanghai. Recently, due to his wife Wang Lanying's illness, he brought her to Shanghai on the 15th of this month to seek medical treatment, staying in Room 1 of the Huaiyang Hotel on North Zhejiang Road. Unexpectedly, at 10 p.m. on the 25th, Zhu Guishou, a ruffian nicknamed "Little Suzhou," accused Wang of being a kidnapper and gathered eight accomplices. Zhu, wielding an axe, rushed into Wang's bedroom and demanded fifty yuan. Wang was penniless but afraid of his power, so he agreed to give him fifteen yuan. He borrowed the money from Chen Ziming, a tea servant at the hotel, but only got ten yuan. He gave the money to Zhu in full, and the remaining five yuan would be paid the next day. Zhu then took the money and left with his accomplices. The next day, Zhu went again to demand the remaining five yuan. At this time, Wang realized that he was being fleeced, so he immediately reported it to the police and was arrested by the Huishi Police Station. Yesterday, he was brought to the Special District Local Court, where Judge Wu Tingqi proposed the case. Wang and his wife appeared in court and explained that they brought his wife to Shanghai for medical treatment and were temporarily staying at the hotel when Zhu falsely accused him of being a kidnapper and gathered accomplices to fleece him. When questioned, the ruffian falsely claimed that he was having an affair with Wang Lanying, so he borrowed ten yuan from her, etc. Judge Wu Tingqi, finding that Zhu Guishou was guilty of extortion, sentenced him to one year and six months in prison as a warning.

Gu Changsheng, a local resident of No. 25, Luban Road in the French Concession, is 26 years old and makes a living by growing vegetables. Every morning, his mother and sister take the produce to sell in the Ximen area. His sister, named Linmei, is 28 years old and has a beautiful appearance, a pretty young lady. She and her mother sell vegetables, going out in the morning and returning at noon, which is their daily routine. However, the other day, her mother fell ill and was bedridden, so Linmei went to sell vegetables alone. For several days in a row, business was quite good. Unexpectedly, a neighboring vegetable stall owner, Hong Chen, an old woman from Shaoxing, is 66 years old. She lives on the Xieqiao Jumen Road. Seeing that Linmei was extremely beautiful and that she was not yet married, she knew that there was a lot of profit to be made, so she enticed her with sweet words every day. Linmei was young and ignorant and was eventually bewitched. On the 8th day of the fifth lunar month, the old woman saw that the time was ripe and took Linmei to live with Chen Tang, a local resident at No. 105 Yangjiazhai, Pudong, to plot to sell her for a good price. Her brother Changsheng saw that his sister had not returned that day and knew that something was wrong, so he inquired around, but found no news. It was not until the other day that he learned from a friend that she had been abducted to Pudong. Linmei had already been betrothed by Hong Chen to a certain person as his wife, with an agreed bride price of 160 yuan. The deal was about to be completed when Changsheng suddenly broke in, ensuring that his sister's chastity was preserved. The person who wanted to buy her saw that things were not going well and immediately slipped away. Wang Yiren is Arrested for Extortion 180

Dr. Wang Yiren's home in Yifeng Lane, Jisi Street, Caojiadu, western Shanghai, received threatening letters from bandits in April of this year, demanding money. Later, he sent his coachman Yan Chaolong to hand over ten dollars to the designated location on Yidingpan Road. On the 24th of this month, he suddenly received another threatening letter, demanding a large sum of money and designating the Andong Hotel in the Public Concession as the contact point. Wang was required to send someone to the hotel first to book a room and write Wang Yiren's name on the water sign. Someone would contact him. After receiving the letter, Wang immediately reported it to the Sixth District Police Station in charge. After receiving the report, District Chief Ren ordered detectives Liu Shaoqing, Tang Bingxiang, and Gan Youxin to disguise themselves and go to the Andong Hotel at 6 p.m. on the 26th, book Room 313, and write Wang Yiren's name on the water sign. At about 8 p.m., a call came to contact them. The bandit claimed that 5,000 yuan was indispensable, and the detectives pretended to be Mr. Zhang, representing Wang, and replied that the amount was too large, and Mr. Wang only had three to four hundred yuan. The bandit then agreed to meet at Room 412 on the fourth floor of the Oriental Hotel. The detectives went as agreed. Unexpectedly, there was no one in that room. They waited for a long time but no one came. The detectives also opened a room to investigate at any time. It was not until after 12 o'clock that they saw a bandit enter the room and sleep peacefully. Detective Liu and others immediately reported to the Old Gate Police Station and sent detectives to join them. At about 6 a.m. the other day, they went to that room and arrested the bandit Huang Yijun. After interrogation by the Special District Court, they were allowed to be transferred. The detectives took the bandit back to the Sixth District Police Station. After interrogation by District Chief Ren, the bandit confessed that his name was Huang Yijun, also known as Ahe, 26 years old, from Songjiang, living at Yongze Third Lane, West Gate, Chenqian Street, jobless. On the afternoon of June 21st, he was smoking in Yanzhiwo, Baoyu Lane, French Concession, when he talked to Chen and Xie Baogen. Xie said that there was a business opportunity, that Wang Yiren, a doctor at Caojiabo Yifeng Lane, could be threatened by letter and extorted a large sum of money. Later, the three of them went to Wuzhen Road, Zhabei, and asked Zhu Jingru to write a letter, which Xie personally sent. It stated that Wang Yiren must book a room at the Andong Hotel and send someone to contact him. On the afternoon of the 26th, I went to Andong to take a look and saw that Wang Yiren had booked Room 313. I was afraid that it was not appropriate, so I went to Taihechun to make a phone call and learned that the representative, Mr. Zhang, had been sent. I said that it must be 5,000 yuan. Mr. Zhang agreed to three or four hundred yuan. I then agreed with Zhang to meet at Room 412 of the Oriental Hotel. Later, I waited outside and saw three or four people coming, whose shape was suspicious, so I went elsewhere. Because the room had already paid the room fee of three yuan, I went to sleep alone at twelve o'clock and was arrested at dawn. District Chief Ren then ordered the coachman Yan Chaolong to identify the bandit, who was indeed the person who had received ten dollars in April. He also ordered the bandit to write numbers, which were the same as the handwriting in the threatening letter. The bandit's threat and extortion were proven to be conclusive, so he prepared a document yesterday and sent the bandit, along with the letter, to the Third Section of the Public Security Bureau for interrogation.
